After completing for you, my sons, this book, which is the final work on medical science with its complement, and having reached the end of it through his expositions and explanations, I saw that it was necessary to complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of practical application, that is, surgery by hand.
Since practical work with the hands has been abandoned in our region and our time: until perhaps its knowledge is lost, and its traces are completely erased; and there remain only small descriptions in old books, which have been altered by hand: and these have suffered errors and uncertainty, until their intentions are misunderstood and their meaning distorted; I saw that it was necessary to revive it with the ordering of this treatise on practical application according to the way of exposition, explanation, and abridgment: and to come with descriptions of the forms of cautery instruments and other tools for the work: which is done by adding explanations and detailing what is necessary.
The reason why a good practitioner of this skill with his own hands is not found in our time is: because the art of medicine is long, and its author must be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy, as described by Galen, until he knows the helpful parts of members, and their shapes, and their joining together, and separation, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, sinews, and their number, and their course, and the pulsating and quiet veins, and the places where they exit.
And for this reason Hippocrates said that the name is great with a name but little with a deed, and especially in the art of the hand.
We have indeed spoken of this in the introduction to this book.
Since those who are not knowledgeable about what we have said regarding anatomy cannot be evacuated without already falling into error, by which people are killed: just as I have seen many of them who are taught in this science and boast themselves about it without knowledge and without experience.
What happened is because I saw a foolish physician cut away a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck and he cut some arteries in her neck: therefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell down dead between his hands.
And I saw another physician who presumptuously attempted to remove a stone from an elderly man, and the stone was large. It therefore happened to him that he removed it along with a piece of the bladder. Therefore, the man died on the third day.
And for my part, I had already been called to remove it; and upon seeing the size of the stone and condition of the patient, I knew he would die.
And I saw another physician who was taking a fee from one of the Dukes of our land for his services: and it happened that a black eunuch who belonged to him suffered a broken leg near the heel; and with great haste, due to his ignorance, the doctor bound up the fracture over the wound with bandages and with strong splints that did not permit any discharge from the injury.
Then he discharged him according to his desires. Afterwards he let him go a few days later and instructed him not to loosen the bandages; and so he stood still until his leg and foot were abscessed, and it came about that he was lost.
I was called to him; I hurried to release the ligament; and tranquility followed, and he escaped from his pains.
However, the corruption was already established in the limb; and I could not restrain it.
Therefore, the corruption ceased to walk about in the limb until it perished.
And I saw another physician who pierced a cancerous abscess; and it became ulcerated after days until its evil was magnified before its owner.
This is because when it is a pure cancer from melancholy humour, then one ought not to approach it with iron at all unless it be in a limb that can bear having the whole of it cut off.
And for this reason, o sons, it is necessary for you to know that operations with the hand are divided into two divisions, namely, an operation associated with a cure and an operation which involves danger in many ways.
And I have aroused you already in every place of this book where an operation comes up which involves fear and dread.
Why it is necessary for you to beware of this and put it aside so that fools do not find a way to talk about it and bring dishonour upon it.
Take therefore the measure with care and protection, and your patients with ease and firmness, and take the better way leading by the grace of God to salvation and commendable succession; and put aside severe illnesses difficult of cure, and remove from yourselves that which makes you afraid so that hesitation does not enter into your faith and your advantage.
It is indeed more beneficial for your glory, and higher status in this world, and ultimately for your wealth.
Galen has indeed said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat an evil disease, lest you be called bad doctors.
I have now divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
Chapter one.
On cauterization with fire and acute medicinal cauterization, categorized by part of the body from head to toe, along with the shapes of instruments and tools for cauterization; and all that is necessary for its execution.
Chapter two.
On incision, perforation, bloodletting and swelling; on the extraction of arrows and similar objects; all categorized by part of the body from head to toe, along with the shapes of instruments and tools.
Chapter three.
On the restoration of bones, their dislocations and treatment for torsion; all categorized by part of the body from head to toe, along with the shapes of instruments and tools.
But before we turn to the actual description of how this is done, it is necessary for me to explain about the harm and benefit of cauterization; on those of complexions for whom it is suitable and at what time; whether with an iron or gold tool.
I say, therefore, that discourse on the quality of cauterization and its harmful effects is extensive, subtle, scientific, and an esoteric secret.
There also spoke a multitude of sages about it, and they disagreed among themselves; as for me, I have had enough from their discourses, fearing the length.
I say, therefore, that cauterization is generally suitable for all constitutions, whether they are with or without matter; excepting two constitutions, which are the warm constitution without matter and the dry one without it.
However, they disagreed about the warm-moist and dry-moist constitutions. For some said that cauterization is beneficial for it. And others said the opposite of this, namely that cauterization is not suitable for an illness caused by heat and dryness; since nature's fire is heat, it is unsuitable to heal a hot-dry illness with hot-dry means.
And he who said the opposite stated that cauterization is beneficial for every hot-dry illness occurring in human bodies; since when you compare a human body and its humours to a fiery constitution, you find the former cold.
And I say according to his discourse, for experience has already proven this to me several times.
However, one ought not to apply it unless he is already proven and practiced in the final exercise of cauterization; has understood the variety of human constitutions, recognized the nature of illnesses within themselves, their causes, incidents, and duration.
Among other constitutions, there is no need to fear for you; especially in regards to cold and moist illnesses. For indeed all physicians have already agreed upon them; and they did not dissent from benefiting with cauterization on these.
And know, my sons, that from the secret of curing with the cautery by fire, and its superiority over the cautery with burning medicine is evident; for fire is simple, whose action does not reach unless to the member which is cauterized: and it does not harm another member joined to it, except with a small injury.
However, the action of burning medicine reaches that which extends from members: and perhaps it causes to happen in the member a difficult-to-heal illness, and perhaps it kills.
But fire, because of its subtlety and goodness of substance, does not do this unless it is excessive.
Indeed, this has become known to us through experience because of the length of our service and study with the art, and our position above truths of things; and I am excused from the length of my words.
And if it were not for the fact that this book of mine does not allow me to bring you the hidden secret in fire and the quality of its operation in bodies by its expulsion, by which it expels illnesses with a demonstrated philosophical discourse sharpened by your minds.
And know, my sons, that they themselves dissent about the time when it is appropriate to perform a cautery, and set a better time according to truth.
And I say that a cautery is appropriate at all times; because any harm caused by the timing is submerged by the benefit gained from the cautery. And especially if the cauterization is due to pains arising from necessary, strong, urgent pains that do not tolerate delay: for it is feared that a greater evil may occur which is more harmful than a slight injury left untreated for some time.
And do not let it enter your minds, O sons, that which is not esteemed, except by the common people and foolish doctors, namely, that for an illness being treated by cauterization, there is not always a relapse: and they assume its consequences, but the matter is not as they think; for cauterization is nothing other than a local medicine, which alters the complexion, and dries up moistures which are causes of pain.
However, cauterization surpasses medicine due to the speed of its cure, and the power of its operation, and the intensity of its dominance: and it is possible that an illness may relapse after some time according to the complexion of the patient, and the location of their illness, and its strength; and also what has been prepared in the body through the accumulation of excesses in it, and what has reached them in their acquisition from food, and similar causes, unless the illness is one where cauterization is administered.
A subtle illness in a limb with few excesses and moistures, such as dental cauterization due to pain, and similar instances can possibly not relapse with that same pain. But this occurs in few cases.
However, the common people's talk that cauterization is the last resort of medicine is correct; not for what they intend in it, because they believe there is no cure which can accompany medicine or anything else after cauterization has been performed.
The reality, however, is the opposite of that, and the intent is that cauterization is the last resort in medicine, not unless we apply the methods of treatment for a particular illness and those medicines do not help; then we use cauterization as a final recourse, and it helps. Thus, it follows that cauterization being the last resort in medicine is not according to the intent understood by the masses and many foolish doctors.
The ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than with iron, and they did not say this unless because of the equality of gold and the loftiness of its substance; and they also stated that a cauterized area does not form pus. But that is not absolutely true; because I have already proven it and found that cauterization does indeed form pus in some bodies but not others.
And cauterization with gold is good and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you ignite the gold cautery tool with fire, it does not indicate to you when it has reached the desired temperature due to the redness of the gold; and when it quickly becomes cold again, if you add more heat to it, it melts into the fire and turns into flakes.
That is why the craftsman falls short with it and, because of this, iron cautery instruments are faster and more convenient for us to use in practice.
And I have indeed arranged this Chapter on cautery according to topics and ordered them from head to toe so as to assist the seeker in finding what they want.
Chapter Two.
The cauterization here is attributed to the dominance of moisture and coldness in the brain: which are two causes of melancholy, and the abundance of humors flowing from the head into the eyes and ears, and an overabundance of sleep, and toothache, and sore throat; and universally every disease that occurs due to coldness, such as paralysis, melancholy, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar ailments.
The method of cauterization is to instruct the patient: to first evacuate their head with a purging medicine for three or four nights, depending on the strength of the patient and his age and habits.
Then instruct them to shave their head with a razor. Then have them sit between your hands in a square position, such that they've already placed their hands on their chest.
Then place the root of your palm on the root of their nose between their eyes. Wherever your middle finger arrives, mark that spot with the cautery iron.
Then fire up the cautery iron, which is of this shape.
Then place the heated iron on that marked spot, pressing it down until your hand is contracted little by little and you're turning it around. Then lift up your hand quickly and inspect the spot.
If you see that the depth of the cauterization has reached the thickness of a bean or the length of fingernail, then lift your hand up. If not, repeat this process with your hand and the same iron instrument or another one if that has become cold; until you see the bones I mentioned to you.
Then take some salt, dissolve it in water, soak the dressing in it, and place it on the wound; leave it for three days.
Then place the dressing soaked in butter on top of it and leave it there until the fire-phlegm is destroyed. Then treat it with the four-ingredient ointment until it is healed.
They have already said that the longer a wound stays open, the more it discharges pus; which is why this way is better and more helpful.
And some of them have said that the skin should be cauterized all the way to the bone; and that the cautery tool must be held there until something solid from the bone burns.
Then after that part of the bone which has been burned is scraped off; it should be treated.
And others say that the cautery must be applied to the very end until it makes a mark on the bone like the imprint of a seal; so that this part of the bone falls out and becomes like a mould for making small bells: or an instrument which women use to stamp letters onto wax; and they believe that vapours from the head come out through this place, so the wound must be left open for a long time.
Then it should be treated until it is healed.
But to me, these two types of cautery do not seem effective except perhaps on people prone to fearful temperaments.
I will let him go, for his well-being is more important to me.
The head weakens due to the disruption of its natural continuity; as we have observed with other body parts. This is especially true when the patient's head is naturally weak and I find the first type of cautery procedure safer and better, so that is what I use. Therefore, proceed with caution for the well-being of the patient.
Head, Chapter 3.
When a patient experiences persistent head pain that continues for an extended period and they have tried various treatments such as herbs, leeches, clysters, oils, and emplastrums without success... And especially if the patient has already been treated with one type of cautery as we described earlier and it has not brought them any relief, then you must consider... But if the patient's head is naturally strong and not weak, yet they experience extreme coldness, then cauterize with a different type of cautery, but only slightly. Cauterize the entire horn of their head with this cautery, but do not penetrate through the skin and expose the amount of bone as we described earlier. Cauterize it with one type of cautery on the back of their head, in the spot known as 'vas', which is where the windpipe is located. Raise your cautery here and do not expose any bone. For the patient will find this pain to be severe and different from the pain of all other types of head cauterizations.
And I shall call this cautery by its proper name: it is a cautery that is used for the horns of the head and the back of the skull; it must be gentler than the one used to cauterize the middle of the head.
Chapter Four.
When pain and swelling occur on one side of the head or extend to the eye, and it is evacuated with cleansers applied to the head, and the rest of the treatment that I mentioned in the classifications of diseases does not bring improvement; then cauterization is performed according to two methods: either with a caustic medicine or with a knife.
The cautery with a caustic medicine is performed by taking one other person's tooth, removing its bark, and cutting off its ends on both sides. Then cut the area of pain at an opportune time with a broad lancet until there is formed beneath the skin a space where the tooth can be placed.
Introduce it beneath the skin until it is hidden; then bind over it with a suitable ligature and leave it for fifteen hours before releasing it, and remove the tooth two or three days later; afterward, apply to it a poultice submerged in butter until the area forms pus; then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to do it with certain caustic medicines that I have written about in the twelfth treatise on Caustic Medicines,
The cauterization with iron is done in this way. Cautery by fire, which has this form.
And it is called a claw because the shape of its head is like that of a nail, which has some curvature, and in the middle there is a small bump.
Then place it on the spot and hold your hand; turn the iron slowly with speed; and let the amount burnt be equal to half its thickness. Raise your hand so as not to burn the artery below and cause bleeding.
Then dip the cautery in salt water and place it on the spot; let it be there for three days; then apply butter; afterwards treat with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicrania with the knife-like end of the cautery. And beware of cutting the artery in this hemicrania, not an old one properly.
On the way of cauterizing an old hemicrania.
When you treat a hemicrania, with what we said in the previous cure, and what we said in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not get better; and you see from the illness that it is not enough for it what we said about the first cautery with medicine, or with fire cautery, then one must use the knife-like cautery until it turns white after you marked on the spot of pain a line whose length is half your finger, or nearly so; and remove your hand once, and press it until you cut the artery, and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuity of the mandible, which moves during chewing, lest the side be burned or the nerve that moves it, whence a spasm may occur.
And be mindful of the cost and caution against arterial blood loss from the severed artery. For its severance entails fear, especially for the one who is ignorant of what they are doing and is neither studious nor experienced, and abandons the operation with him first.
And I shall come with the reminder of the treatment for accidental arterial bleeding as it is described and in its place in this book.
If you see from the ailment that it is not sufficient for this cautery and you see the patient's body enduring the cautery at the center of the head as we described, tend to the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, apply the cautery as we said in the chapter on arterial ligation with a cautery having two blades. For this type of cauterization is better and more effective.
On the method of cauterizing earache.
When there is an earache due to cold and it is treated with a solution and the remaining treatment we described in the section on external applications, and the pain is not removed, then use a cautery by fire: and this is what is called a Point, whose form is thus.
Then make points with it after its ignition all around the ear as it is turned; or all around either one if pain is simultaneously in both. And extend yourself with the caustic iron from the root of the ear for a moment, after you have marked the places with the encaustic; and let the amount of the caustic be ten points on each ear, and so forth.
Then treat those places until they are healed.
The method of cauterization for the torticollis.
Chapter Seven.
The torticollis that is treated with cauterization is not anything but the kinds which happen from excess phlegm, according to what we have said about the divisions of illnesses.
And turn the cauterization towards the kind that happens from desiccation and nerve spasm.
When you treat this kind of torticollis with eardrops and head-purgings and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three caustic irons: one near the root of the ear, a second just below the earlobe, and a third at the joining of the two lips.
And place your caustic iron on the opposite side of the affected part. Because softening does not happen unless it appears on a healthy part.
And the form of this kind of cauterization is that you cauterize with a caustic iron at the outer edge of the upper ear, just below the horn of the head; and again on the earlobe itself, whose length should be according to the length of your thumb. And leave your hand with the caustic iron until half the thickness of the skin has been burnt.
And this is the shape of a cautery, and it is a type made from a surgical knife, whose form was presented above; however, it is not any finer than that, as you can see: and there should be a knife inside it that is slightly thicker than usual.
Then treat the places with what has preceded; until it heals.
A paragraph on the method of cauterizing an old apoplectic condition.
When an old apoplectic condition is treated and you treat it with what we have said, and your treatment does not help, and the patient has no fever, then cauterize them with four cauteries over each corner of their head, and one in the middle of the head, as we have said, and one at the back of the head, according to what has preceded; and make the cautery according to what has been said before.
It is also cauterized with a cautery over the mouth of the stomach; and this is more effective.
Then it should be treated with what has been said before.
Chapter 9.
It is necessary that the patient first be given large amounts of liquor, and cleansing pills for the brain.
Then shave the patient's head entirely, and place on their occipital bone a plaster of mustard seed described in the treatise on plasters; and put it there several times.
For this is the way of cauterization; and do it in the same manner that I have described there.
If it heals through this, it is good. If not, then perform three cauterizations on the back of their head, which should extend from the top of the head down to the lower part of the eye; and leave a finger's width between each cauterization.
Then treat the cauterizations with the same method as before.
If you wish to add more and the patient can tolerate it, then perform a cauterization in the middle. If you wish to add more, cauterize it above the two corners (i.e., the temples).
Then treat it until it heals; let the cauterization be oiled according to the form which has been described.
On the method of cauterizing for paralysis and softening (i.e., scar tissue).
Chapter 10.
It is necessary to proceed with cleansing the head using urine, and what we have said before (i.e., cauterization).
Then shave the patient's head; afterwards cauterize it with a cauterization in the middle of the head, and one above each corner of the head, and one at the back, and three on the vertebrae of the neck.
If you need to soften the patient's body in many places because of a strong illness, and they can tolerate it: then cauterize them with four cauterizations on the vertebrae of their back; and for the last one, burn through as much skin as possible, but raise your hand before causing injury. Then treat it until it heals; oil the cauterization in this way.
The method of cauterization for epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized unless it is one whose epilepsy arises from phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary that you cleanse his brain first with hyoscyamus, and with the other treatment we mentioned in the division; when the patient is large or can tolerate the acceptance of medicines.
But if it is a child who cannot tolerate medicines, then give him gargles and cleansing chews for the brain, many days beforehand with an improvement of diet.
Then shave his head and afterwards cauterize it with a cautery once on the middle of the head as previously mentioned; with another one on the back of his head, and over every corner of his head. If the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then cauterize him with the cauteries that I mentioned in having paralysis, and soften his body over the vertebrae of the neck and the back; and let the cautery be olive-oil as described previously.
But if the patient is a child then put on a fine cautery in this way.
Chapter 12.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupt humours and thick phlegm then cauterize it with the cauteries that we mentioned for having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess downwards to the melancholy and the body of the patient is moist, then give him in drink something that cleanses his brain as mentioned previously; afterwards shave the head of the patient and make a pad from decently made linen like a circle.
Then place it on the middle of the head; and let the patient sit square being held from every side.
Then present the ointment. And it is more worthy from old egg butter. And warm it over a fire with moderate heat, as much as the finger can bear when inserted into it. Then evacuate it onto the middle of their head in a circle, and leave it until it cools.
Do this to the patient once every week along with the rest of their good regimen until they are healed.
Or if you wish, cauterise it by making very small multiple points on it, except for where you hold the hand with the cauteriser: let it be fumigated below.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with moisture.
Then place on it a poultice soaked in butter or chicken fat.
On the method of cauterising downwards towards the eye.
Chapter 13.
When you are told that there is a beginning of water in the eye by signs, which I mentioned in the division, then begin and let the patient drink with what cleanses their head.
And keep them away from all moisture, and make them sit in a bath fasting for some days.
Then instruct him to scrape his head, and cauterise it on the middle of their head. Then cauterize it above the two temples with two cauterizations, if there is an onset of water drainage from both eyes at once; or from one side, if there is water drainage from one eye only: and cut off with the cauterization all the veins and arteries that are under the skin; and let the cauterizations be as long as the width of the temples; and beware of any bleeding.
If you see anything coming out of it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible; and I will come with wisdom regarding the extraction of arteries, their cutting, and caution against bleeding.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, below the two bones, with two cauterizations applied at the very end.
On the method of cauterizing for old tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and persistent: and they appear on the veins and arteries that are visible on the outside of the head, it is verified that this is due to excess cold and phlegmatic humors; then cauterize with the same cauterization method I described at the beginning for water drainage, applying a cauterization in the middle of the head, two cauterizations above the two temples, and two cauterizations on the neck below the two bones. And if you require additional treatment, then cauterize it carefully on every side of the eye, at the end of the eyebrow with a small cauterization tool.
On the method of cauterizing for nasal odor.
When you treat it with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not take effect; then hasten and give him an infirmocochias potion for three nights: then shave his head and cauterize it with a central cauterization using an olive oil cauterizer. Then cauterize it with two clavicle-shaped cauteries, above the two eyebrows a little under the hair.
And guard against the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the shape of the clavicle cautery.
On the method of cauterizing a softened eyelid.
When the eyelid of an eye softens due to illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with a single cautery, with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries on each side; and they extend from the two temples: and let the length of every cautery be according to the lengths of the eyebrow; and do not remove your hand with the cautery, but according to the amount that is burned away of the third eyelid.
On the method of cauterizing an eyelid with inverted hairs that irritate the eye.
The cautery is of two kinds; either with fire, or with a caustic medicine.
But in the case of a fire cautery, tell the patient beforehand to let his hair grow if he is one who keeps it clean-shaven, until they lengthen and equalize. If however they prick him at their roots, then bind his eyes with a cloth so that they do not move until they are born.
When they are born and equalized, then place the patient's head in your lap; next, brand over their eyelids with a cautery iron, marking it in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and let the beginning of the brand be near the eyelashes.
Next, place over their eye a poultice soaked in egg white; or use linseed mucilage instead.
Then heat the following type of iron with fire.
Next sear the skin around that mark with many slow touchings of the iron until its surface blisters over completely in the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And you will see your operation has been successful when the eyelid is seen to twitch and the eyelashes by it rise up.
So raise your hand then, and let them go after three days.
Next place over this a poultice with butter in it until the scar is sloughed away. Then treat them with an ointment until they recover.
If any of the eyelashes grow back afterwards and the eyelid becomes flabby, then repeat the cautery on that place as you did at first.
But if the eyelashes are on their lower lid, then sear it until they rise up to their proper place; and equalize them so that the lashes do not prick the eye.
Let it be that you advise the patient to leave hair alone until it grows back and becomes even again. Make from cloth a piece of paper shaped like a myrtle leaf.
Then take of known soap and of lime not slaked from each one ounce in weight or as much as that; then pound them together well and make it with haste so that it does not cool down. Then spread from that onto the paper you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf and place it over one eyelid or two. And put under the eye wool soaked in egg white; and let the patient's head be in your lap.
And put your index finger on top of the medicine and press it down for a moment. And you will move it as often as the patient feels a sting from the medicine because its sting is like fire.
While therefore he persists with this thing which he found to be a sting, then leave the medicine and move it with your finger. When therefore the sting calms down then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And consider then if you see the eyelid is raised like it has been with fire or with a cut; and if not then repeat on it the medicine where the medicine did not stick, nor darken until your operation becomes even and the eye contracts.
Then put on it wool with butter until burnt skin is removed. Then treat it with diaphanicon ointment, or another, until it is healed.
And when performing the operation, you must be careful to protect the patient's eye, lest any of the medicine fall into it.
If the eyelid becomes softened after a few days and there is still something fighting to come out of the eye, then repeat the application of medicine on that specific area which has become soft due to the eyelid, as you did initially. Then treat it until it is healed.
And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And you should know that human eyes vary in size and smallness. Therefore, let your consideration be according to that: the way of righteousness is not hidden from one who has a zeal for this art.
On the method of cauterizing a fistula in the tear duct.
When you treat a fistula as we described in the section on diseases and your treatment does not take effect, then it is necessary that you cauterize it in this way.
Instruct the patient to place their head in your lap and have your assistant hold their head securely between their hands so that it cannot be moved or shaken.
Then place a caustic paste made of gallnut extract or flaxen mucilage on their eye; afterwards, use this form of cautery instrument.
Let it be a hollow cautery like the shape of an eagle's quill feather from one end with which the cautery is done; and if you want to make it penetrating right through to the other end, so do it. If you wish to make its point upwards, so do that instead.
However, this cavity is better for your operation.
Next squeeze the abscess, if it is open, and remove its purulent fluid, then dry it out; and if it is not open, then open it up, and extract its pus.
Then place upon it a very hot cautery.
And hold your hand with it for a moment near the cautery from the eye, towards the side of the nose, so that your hand does not stray, or the patient is disturbed; and place the cautery on the fat of the eye, and burn it.
If therefore you penetrate with your cautery right up to the bone, then that will be good. And if not: then repeat the cautery once or twice, if you need to; and leave it for three days.
Then apply a poultice with butter, and treat it with drying ointment until it is healed.
But if forty days elapse and it does not heal: then place on it a caustic medicine until the bone is exposed; and scrape it according to what was said in your chapter.
And there is another method of cautery for abscesses, which some ancients have described. Attend to the place of the abscess, and find it; then place into its fissure a slender probe, that is, a fine cannula, whose form is this: [illustration]. And pour into it the quantity of a drachma's worth of molten lead, and hold your hand with the cannula firmly, and do not let the patient move at all, so that [the lead] does not run or reach his eye.
You must place a poultice infused with egg white over the patient's eye, or in water.
For lead burns the site of the fistula, and heals it with a wondrous healing.
If the fistula is healed, with what we have said about cauterization and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer a nasal hole, and redirect the fistula towards the nose's passage, according to what will come to its proper place.
On the method of cauterizing cracks in the lips.
Cracks often occur in the lip, which are called "pili," especially in the lips of children.
When you treat these cracks, as we have said in the division of ailments, and the treatment does not take effect, then use a small knife-shaped cauterizer with fire, according to this form.
And let it be hollowed out according to the thinness of the knife.
Then place it, burning hot, quickly into the cracks themselves, until the cauterization reaches the deepest part of the crack.
Then treat it with a caustic [substance], until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing an oral fistula.
When an abscess happens at the root of the gums, or on the palate, or at the roots of teeth: then it makes pus and ruptures; afterward, it festers and runs with pus, and becomes a fistula: then you treat it, but the treatment does not take effect in it, then you must use a cauterizer according to its size which will fit into the fistula. Insert the heated iron into the opening of the fistula and hold your hand there until the hot iron reaches its depth and end; do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards with what we have said about the treatment until it is healed.
If therefore the pus discharges and heals, it will be good. And if it does not heal, then you must uncover the location and remove the rotten bone as will come to its head.
On the method of cauterizing gums and softened teeth.
When the gums are softened by moisture, and the teeth become loose, and you treat them with medicine but it does not help; then place the patient's head in your lap.
Then use the cautery fire with this shape, so that you place a pipe over the tooth; and quickly insert in it a heated cauterizer: and hold your hand there for some time until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of their tooth.
And lift your hand; then repeat the cautery several times as you wish.
Then have the patient fill their mouth with salt water, hold it there for an hour; and spit it out.
For the loose tooth is firmed, and the softened gums tighten, and the corrupted moisture dries up.
On the method of cauterizing for toothache.
When tooth pain is due to coldness, or there are worms within and treatment with medicine does not help, then cauterization on the tooth itself is done in two ways: either cauterization with butter, or cauterization with fire.
The cauterization with butter is done by taking goat's butter and boiling it in an iron spoon or pot. Next, take the cauterizing instrument (a red-hot iron) and wrap it with a cloth at its end. Then dip the instrument into the boiled butter and quickly place it on the painful tooth, holding it there until it cools down. Repeat this several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth.
If you wish, you may also dip wool or a cloth into cold butter and place it on the aching tooth; then put a red-hot iron on top of that until the heat reaches deep inside the cavity of the tooth.
The cauterization with fire is done by applying either an air pipe or an iron pipe to the area. If there is any thickness on the body of the patient which prevents the sharpness of the fire from reaching their mouth...
Next, take the fire cautery of this shape and place it on that tooth; hold your hand there until the cautery cools down.
Repeat this several times; for the pain will be relieved either that same day or on the next day.
The patient should fill their mouth with good butter to cover the mark of the cautery and hold it there for an hour; then spit it out.
And this is the form of cauterization.
Cauterize with any end you wish according to what is possible: and this is the form of the cannula.
On the method of cauterizing with a hot iron.
When the ulcers are due to phlegm and cold humours, and they do not yield to medicinal treatment, and you wish to bring about their quick cure: then use a concave cautery of this form.
Having two tight ends so that the smoke may come out at one end of the cautery: and place it burning on the ulcer once or twice if you need to until you reach the bottom of the ulcer.
But if the ulcer is small: then place the cautery according to the size of the ulcer.
Then leave it for three days, and place on it cotton soaked in butter until what the fire burnt is removed.
Then treat it with tooth-alkali ointment until the form of the cannula heals.
On the method of cauterizing for hoarseness of voice and shortness of breath.
When humours gather over the trachea and especially when there is coldness of constitution, then it ought to be evacuated first by means of dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it by night at the root of the throat in a hollow place: and take care not to reach with the cautery the gullet nor the skin unless some of it.
Then cauterize it with another cautery near the neck joint at his last vertebra, finishing [the operation]: and let the cautery be a clavicle-shaped one similar to the previous one.
Then treat it with what preceded until it heals.
On the method of cauterization for lung disease and cough.
When cough and lung disease are caused by cold humors, the patient has no fever nor any sign of phthisis, and it is an old disease: then cauterize them with two cauteries above the clavicle in shallow, soft, empty spots. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between two nipples: and let this second cautery be cannula-shaped like the previous one.
And if you wish your cauterization to be performed by pricking with a cautery called "the Point", whose shape was mentioned earlier for earache pricking: and let the number of points be from thirty up until almost forty.
Then treat it with what preceded until it heals.
And now let the cautery have three branches: like this shape. Why is the cautery mitigated with what you do with three cauteries at once?
Chapter 27.
When the head of the humerus is dislocated because of moisture and it does not return to its place at once upon being relocated until it becomes accustomed to returning, then it dislocates from a slight movement as we have already testified that this happens, then you should relocate the joint first. The patient should then lie down on their back, or on their healthy side. Then elevate the skin that is inside the elbow towards the upper part with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint is dislocated inwardly.
Then have a cauterizing fire with two rods. Its form is as follows.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side, and there will appear a figure of cauterization with four cauteries.
And sometimes the cauterization is done with a cautery having three rods, so that the figure of cauterization appears as six cauteries; and the rods are chosen according to their fineness.
And this is the form of the three-rod cautery.
And sometimes one is added to this configuration, resulting in eight cauteries.
Then place crushed leeks with salt on the cautery. Then make sure to keep the patient calm so that they do not move their limbs until they are healed.
And if the dislocation is upward, which happens rarely, then you should cauterize it on the shoulder with a ball-shaped cautery, or by pricking it with several small cauteries.
For the joint is made firm again, moisture removed; and the patient heals.
On the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When there is coldness and excessive moisture in the stomach until it is removed from its own constitution, and catarrhs begin to increase towards it, and frequent modes of treatment are applied without benefit: then the patient should be laid supine on their back with their legs and arms outstretched. Then cauterize with three cauterizations; with a sub-spoonful cautery of the chest the size of one finger alongside a clavicle cautery, and two additional cauteries below from either side by one cautery until the shape of the cauterization becomes triangular. And leave some space between each so that they do not join up when they produce pus.
And the depth of the cauterization should be two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And the shape of the cauterizations should be as follows without addition, and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach it should be shaped thusly; let the device that performs this cauterization have one circular shape like so.
And the stomach is cauterized by being pricked with a needle which has been heated red-hot in this cautery; and it will be done such that you prick onto the stomach as many times as desired with an iron; then cauterize each spot with a single point cautery; afterwards treat each of them according to the treatment prescribed until they are healed.
On the method of performing a cold cauterization on the spleen:
When there is pain in the spleen due to coldness and moisture, or from thick wind, until it leaves its natural constitution with an excessive discharge, and the patient is treated as we have said but makes no progress; then they should be laid supine on their neck, and you should mark out three cauteries like so, of this size, at the same place beneath the spleen from where a man's elbow reaches down to: let there be between each one a space equal to the thickness of a finger, and let them all be as long as a straight line; do not press your hand very much on the cautery.
And let the amount that is cauterized be in proportion to the thickness of the skin, with half its size not added; and let the patient stand on his own feet.
But if he cannot stand, then let him lie down, having already stretched out his legs and raised his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is indeed possible for you to use these knife-cautery techniques with the actual cautery iron when you have skill and wisdom in this art.
And be careful not to go too far in your cauterization, and that you do not burn through the entire thickness of the skin, for if you do it will burn the whole body and reach the intestines: for the skin there is thin, so you must know this.
On the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
When it happens and you wish to know whether the abscess is in the liver's flesh or its capsule, then if it is in the liver's flesh, the patient feels a dull pain with weight but no sharpness; and if it is in the liver's capsule there is pain that has severe acuteness: and already you see how wearisome this cure was to his physicians.
Therefore, the patient must lie on their back with their neck exposed. Next, mark the abscess site with an ink-burn; then take a fire-heated cautery iron that is like a rod. And this is its form. Cauterize with that one iron until all the skin is burned and it reaches the bone, until all pus has come out; then cure this with the cure for discharging sores, until he is healed.
And one should not use this type of cauterization unless their studies in the art of medicine are prolonged, and these ailments have rushed through their hands with some experimentation; then indeed will they dare to perform such an operation.
But as for letting it go, in my view, it is better with me.
[Regarding] the method of cauterization in [the case of] pleurisy.
The ancients said, "Cauterization with the roots of *Aristolochia* for cold pleurisy in this way. And it is such that you should take from the dry roots of *Aristolochia*, one longer root which is found within, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil, and light it on fire. Then cauterize with one large cauterizer where the collar bone meets the neck, and two small ones slightly sloped downwards towards the side which is under the jaw.
And with two more cauterizers on the spot between the fifth and sixth ribs sloped slightly towards the back, one in the center of the chest, and another over the stomach. And three more from behind; one between the shoulder blades, and two on either side of the chest, the lower one again being between the shoulder blades.
And you must not press your hand with the cauterizer, rather it should be held away from the skin, sniffing the smell.
And some ancients have said that there are those who use an iron cauterizer like a radius (a bone in the forearm); they light it on fire and insert it between the ribs until they reach the abscess, and pus flows out, as we have said with regard to liver abscesses.
But in this perforation, when using a caustic, there is the fear that either the patient dies immediately or a fistula occurs in the place, which has no cure.
On the method of cauterizing the spleen - Chapter 32.
When you are treating a spleen disease, as we have mentioned previously when discussing the different types of illnesses, and your treatment is not effective, then cauterization on it can be done in three ways, all of which are appropriate.
One of which is to make three or four caustic applications by lining them up along the length of the spleen according to the shape of the liver cauteries described previously.
And let there be between each caustic application an amount equal to the thickness of a finger or more or less.
And let the method of caustic application be as described for liver cauteries equally.
And do not press your hand when applying the caustic; let the patient be lying prone on their back.
Another method of cauterization is to use a caustic with two prongs as we described in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder: and lift the skin that is over the spleen where the patient's left elbow reaches; and let your lifting be such that you raise the skin according to the width of their body so that the caustics fall along the length of the body.
Then introduce the two ignited prongs until you pierce through the skin on the other side; then withdraw the caustic; thus four caustics are made.
And if you wish to use another type of caustic with three prongs.
Then treat the cautery after you discharge it to emit pus for many days: it is more beneficial than the rest of what preceded in the cure.
On the method of cauterizing with hydropsy.
The cautery does not fall out in hydropsy unless it is proper to the ascites.
When you treat hydropsy with the methods of treatment that we have mentioned in the division and the cure does not improve, then it is necessary for you to cauterize it with four cauteries around the navel, one cautery over the stomach, another over the liver, a third over the spleen, two behind the back between the vertebrae, one directed at the chest, and the other at the stomach: and let the depth of the cautery be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the open cautery so that it emits pus for a long time.
And you will not discharge the patient from treatment after the cautery with it, which must be applied to him twice: and healing will hasten towards it with God's help.
The shape of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be a nail according to its previous form; and that of the one used for the back an olive-leaf according to its former shape.
On the method of cauterizing feet and legs.
When there are blisters on the hydropsy and they are filled with yellow water, you must cauterize over the back of the foot in the night-watch between the auricular and annular [phalanges]: then raise your hand with the cautery and do not twist it; afterwards raise your hand, and do not repeat it at all.
The yellow water should be boiled and used as a caustic in this form.
Then make two caustic irons over the two legs, with a knife-shaped tip on each iron; and let one of these be made according to the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other beneath that one, roughly in the middle of the leg; and then two more caustics over the entire thigh. Leave the irons open for some time without treatment: so as a little water may boil out of them: then treat it with the rest which we mentioned earlier.
On how to cauterize an open belly wound.
Chapter 35.
When an open belly wound is caused by cold and moisture, until it weakens the retentive and digestive faculties which are in the stomach and intestines; and when you treat it with conventional remedies but it does not heal: and you see a patient bearing the caustic iron on account of his superabundant vitality, then cauterize him with a large caustic iron over his belly as mentioned before for cauterizing the stomach with a circular caustic iron, and four small caustic irons around the navel, with a needle-like caustic iron; and with one or two large caustic irons on top of the alchosos.
And if you see abundant moisture and the patient bearing it well, then cauterize him with a caustic iron over the spine; and another one over the entire flank: perhaps also adding two small caustic irons on top of the belly near the large one.
It is indeed a successful treatment where its benefit does not go astray.
On how to cauterize haemorrhoids.
Chapter 36.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus or just one that is caused by thick, cold, and corrupt humors, and it does not heal when treated as we said before: then cauterize with three cauteries on the lower spine below the shoulder blades a little triangularly, and with another cautery under the navel about two fingers long.
And if you think that their stomach is chilled and the food is not being digested, and you see that their face has pustules, then cauterize them on their stomach with a large cautery as previously described; also with another cautery above their liver, and one over their spleen, along with one at the clavicle: leave the cauteries open for some time. Then treat them until they are healed.
Chapter 37.
When you excise the hemorrhoids, then ignite a cautery that resembles a spoke. Then insert the ignited cautery into the excised hemorrhoid; and keep your hand there until you reach the opening of the vein from which blood is flowing: do this once or twice.
If therefore there are many hemorrhoids, then cauterize each one with a cautery as we have described. Then treat them with salves that suit them until they are healed.
And if you cauterize with a large cautery over the navel, it is more effective for improvement.
The method of cauterizing a fistula in ano.
Chapter XXXVIII.
When the patient does not obey the incision and operation that we have described in its proper place, and is afraid of it, he may perhaps be cured with a cauterization.
So when someone gets a fistula and it becomes old, pus runs from it, and there are corrupted fluids. It is appropriate then that you should examine it with a thin probe. Then determine the depth of it with the probe.
Next heat up the circular cautery. Then introduce yourself, heated, into the fistula itself, for as long as the probe went in.
And repeat the cautery on it, until they burn all those corrupted parts of the body - once or twice or three times, depending on how much is necessary.
And beware of burning the nerve if it is there or a large vein - or if the fistula goes into the body of the bladder or the intestines, then take care from all these places.
And do not do it unless the fistula is in fleshy tissue and you think that it will not penetrate.
Then look after the place until it is healed.
But if the place is sealed up, and materials are cut off from it, and this remains so for a long time - then you know that he has now been thoroughly healed.
And if they do not cut away the matter from it, then know that it is penetrating, or there is a corrupted bone deep inside, or almost like one of those: whose description will come in its place.
On the method of cauterising kidneys.
When there is pain in the kidneys due to cold or thick windiness and it weakens because of that, then one ought to cauterise them over almethenem on top of the kidneys themselves with a clavicle cautery, whose description has preceded this.
And perhaps we cauterise it again within the almeidat itself. Why three lined ones will come. Thus they shall be more beneficial as the last resort.
On the method of cauterising the bladder.
When there is weakness and softening in the bladder due to cold and moisture such that the afflicted person cannot hold urine, then one ought to cauterise it on the lower part of suminis over the bladder where hair starts to grow with a right-handed sumin cautery and another from its left; and let its length be according to the size of the thumb's knuckle; and cauterise it further down the back with one or two cauteries if needed, and let them be as per the preceding clavicle cautery.
On the method of cauterising the uterus.
When cold and dampness occur in the uterus, preventing conception, and her menses are corrupted, and their onset is delayed, and she experiences pain at their arrival, then she ought to be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of vesico-uterine fistula, and a cautery below the back over the sacrum, or two cauteries; and let the cautery be clavicle-sized.
On the method of cauterizing the ancle in dislocation.
When the mucous moistures are poured out onto the ancle-bone and become the cause of its exit from its place; and its sign is that the leg is lengthened over the other when they are compared with each other, and the place of dislocation is found to be empty in it.
It is necessary therefore that you cauterize the weak above the ancle-bone with a cautery of similar circle: after you have marked it with encaustics around the ancle, as it rotates; and so that the bone itself falls into the middle of the circle.
But if this cautery is not present to you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large oil-lamp cautery; and let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of all the skin.
Then treat it until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing sciatica.
When there is pain in the hip joint and its cause is cold and moisture: treat the patient with what we have said in the section on divisions, but if treatment does not help and the problem persists, you must then relieve the patient of thick humors using foul-smelling pills or artificial pills and similar substances. Then cauterize them.
And there are two methods of cauterization: either with medications that burn or with fire.
Cauterization by fire is done in many ways.
One of which is to place three triangular cauterizations on the hip joint in this shape. And make them either deep or shallow. The space between each cauterization should be the width of a finger, and they should be made with an olive-oil cautery iron.
Sometimes there is also a cauterization in the center, right above the head of the hip joint. Because these four cauterizations form a cross-shape.
And if you want to cauterize with a circle, whose form was previously used in the cauterization of hip dislocations, ensure it is a circle that contains the entire hip joint.
Burn away all the thick skin entirely.
This is the method of cauterization for sciatica when there is pain attached to the hip joint that does not reach as far as the thigh and leg.
However, if it does extend to the thigh and leg, then cauterize them with two cauterizations on the thigh over the spot where they indicate pain is present; add your own fourth cauterization four fingers from the extremity using a knife-shaped iron.
The depth of the cauterization should correspond to the thickness of the skin.
If the patient indicates that the pain extends close to their toes, then cauterize them there where they indicate with a point, three, four, or more cauterizations, as required.
And if they indicate the pain is below the knee towards the leg, then cauterize them there with a single knife-like cauterization.
And take care in all your cauterizations not to go so far with the cauterization that you burn a nerve or large artery and cause great harm or contraction to the patient through it.
And I myself have seen one and another, among those who cauterized above the shin and overdid it in their cauterization, and the leg became swollen until the swelling reached the foot, and it was all perforated and completely corrupted; then there occurred a rupture of the belly and death afterwards.
If the pain is in two places at once, cauterize both in this way.
And some wise men have said about the cauterization of the hip that this is its method. Make a tube-like instrument from iron whose diameter is half the width of your palm; and let it be at its opening as thick as a thumb or slightly less; and inside this instrument there should be another smaller one.
And let the space that is between each instrument be of the length of a knuckle; and they should all have openings at both ends; and their height should be as long as one or two knuckles; and attach a handle to them made from iron, which fits awkwardly.
Then it is heated in fire until it reddens and throws sparks; then it is placed on an earthenware vessel with the weak lying down propped up on the healthy side. Therefore, cauterize him with three round cauteries one after another.
Then leave him alone for three days. Later, apply ointments with butter; and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
Albucasis says, with this type of cauterization, my sons, we have used it rarely due to the fear of its appearance; and also because there are few whom we find willing to endure it.
However, it is among the good cauterizations for him who endures it; and he will find its place.
But if you want to make a cautery with medicinal smokes, then make two pieces of wood having a perforated ring into which descends the hinge of its door made out of brass or iron as long as the wall; and at their height let there be two knots, or something similar.
And let there be the space between each one of the thickness of a finger; and let them be open at the bottom and top; and let them fit into each other according to this form.
Then place it on the earthenware vessel with the weak lying down propped up on the healthy side. And press your hand hard over the earthenware vessel. Next, immerse the two circles in warm water, which has been heated for a short while with fire, and hold it there for an hour's time; the patient can withstand its bite and burning since he finds its bite like that of fire until the biting stops.
Next, lift your hand with the instrument, and wipe off the warm water from the entire wound with fresh water; then leave it there for three days.
And place butter on top of it until the blackness of burning is removed; leave it there for a few days and pus will drain from it. For this is indeed the last part of treatment.
Next treat it with ointments until it heals.
But if the pain extends to the hip or leg; make for him an apparatus on that part which contains water, as you did for the wound equally.
And this is the method of warm water; and I have already written it down in my book on medicinal preparations. Take one part alkali and one part unslaked lime; grind both of them, and put them in a new pot whose lower part has a single small hole according to the size that will be taken up by this radius; place under the base of the pot another worn-out pot; throw over the alkali and the lime from fresh water which should submerge both by one finger's breadth; after you have pressed it down with your hand firmly; leave the pot until cold water comes out of the lower part of the worn-out pot.
Next collect all that water and throw it over another lime; stir until it is renewed.
It will then have great sharpness, which is applied to many medical procedures and to the cauterisation of other body parts. Because it makes fire do its job.
And from medicine are those with which they cauterise the ankle, just like with thuya and nut butter, and lime mixed with soap so that both can be applied together.
Galen indeed told the story of a man from ancient times whose treatment cured ankle and sciatic vein pain, and praised its effectiveness greatly. He said that no other treatment was needed and he had healed in one go until he told how the man perhaps entered a bath carried by others and left it completely healed.
And it is to be made from green thuya and if not found fresh then take the dry one instead; grind a lot of this with some fat and apply it over where the pain is whether ankle, leg or hip bone: bandage this on and leave for three hours but let the patient remove when they feel enough burning. Then put him into the bath.
When his body is then moistened, place him on a couch. For the pain goes away and he heals.
And you should know that no one must use the cautery with these medicines unless after a bowel movement.
And Dioscorides who said this also stated that goat droppings, when mixed with the above and used to cauterise a sciatic vein, help it heal; and so is made this kind of cautery. Let wool be taken and soaked in old oil, then placed on the deep spot which is between the big toe and the next one, closest to the latter.
Then take dry goat dung and set it on fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place the charcoal over the wool and leave it there until it is extinguished. Then repeat this process. Keep doing it until sensation returns to the ankle area via touch and the pain subsides.
And this method of cauterization is called Goat-Brand Cautery.
On the cauterization of back pain:
Back pain can arise from many causes, such as strain, blows or excessive discharge, and by the introduction of cold moist matter; cauterization is only used for this last type of pain.
It is therefore necessary to apply foul pills and the like on the back, over three lines of width corresponding with the patient's waist, after which you mark each line with five cauteries or more according to the amount that comes out depending upon the endurance of the patient; perform a needle-cautery cauterization.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries in a central row, according to this pattern: [insert illustration of the pattern].
On the method of cauterization for beginning hump formation:
This illness occurs many times in small children.
And the sign of its onset in children is: that it happens to him with a tightness during breathing upon elevation and movement; and you find at the lower end of the spine and its knots, which has now begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When therefore you see it, and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a cautery which is a circle of this shape.
And let the cautery take hold over the entire area of the vertebra equally; and if you wish to cauterize around the vertebra, use a point cautery in two or three lines, and let the points be close to each other.
Then treat the place until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware, do not apply the cautery to a hump which forms from a nerve spasm.
On the method of cauterization for podagra and joint pains.
When joint pains are from cold moist humours which are poured into any part of the body; then when they happen in the feet it is customary for physicians to call this podagra specifically.
When therefore podagra from cold causes is treated with therapeutic methods, and the pains are not removed; then the cautery removes them.
And it is as if you cauterize him after evacuation around the joints of the feet with multiple cauteries; and let the cautery be an Olive-shaped one.
And if you need to make an incision on the surface of the foot, then make punctures with the cautery. But if the pains ascend to the knees or other joints and this often happens, then cauterize it over the entire knee with three cauteries, or four on all sides, using the same Clavulanic cautery.
If however you need more of this cautery, then cauterize it further. And do not immerse your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about as thick as the skin.
If however the pains ascend to the knees and back: then apply what we have said about the cautery in its own chapter.
If the pains are in the hands alone, then make incisions around the wrists where two lines revolve.
If any of the pain remains in the fingers, then make incisions on them, over every knuckle with an incision and over the comb of the hand.
If however the pains ascend after days to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both on all sides.
And do not discharge the sick person from their good diet or from taking their medicines. For if a good diet is kept and the phlegm is discharged, he will be cured by God's help with this cautery.
On the method of cauterization for ruptures.
When there is a rupture in the groin and the intestine or caecum descends towards the testicle and it begins to draw near, then you must instruct the patient to fast for one day. And he should use laxatives so that the stool descends from his abdomen.
Then have him sit between your hands on his back and tell him to hold his breath until either the caecum or intestine comes out.
Then bring it back with your fingers and mark with cauterizer under the rupture on the pectineal bone with a sign whose end is similar to half of a circle at the top of the body.
Then heat the cautery of this shape until it turns white and starts to give off sparks. Then return the caecum or intestine to its cavity. Then have the assistant put his hand over this place so that the intestine does not come out: and you now open between the patient's legs, placing a pillow under him and another servant holding down the patient's legs while one holds their hands on their chest.
Then place the cautery back over that mark with your hand holding it straight. And hold it there until you reach the bone with it or repeat this process again if you did not reach the bone on your first attempt.
Carefully observe the exit of the intestine when you are cauterizing, lest you burn it and cause either death or great harm to come upon the patient.
And you should understand that when your cauterization does not reach the bone then this operation is of no benefit.
The tool should be delicate and proportionate to their size for infants.
Then treat it with the rest of the ointments until it is healed.
And if he has been lying on his back for forty days until the wound seals over.
You must provide nourishment for the length of his treatment with a gentle food to ease his stomach; so that it doesn't leave his intestines during straining and defecation.
Then when he wishes to get up after forty days, then apply a bandage made too loose and keep it on for another forty days.
He should be spared from work, and over-eating or drinking, and shouting loudly.
For when he follows this regimen, thus he recovers with a complete recovery.
And I shall describe the treatment of ruptures involving incisions in its own chapter.
When however ruptures occur in the rest of the belly and are starting out, if you wish that they not spread, then cauterize his rupture with a round cautery according to its size; and let what is burned be from there on like one third of it. Then treat it with that which we have described; and it will not spread.
And now some early writers have said that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery in this shape.
After it is sealed with caustic, and you place a line which runs across the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. Place your hand in the middle with a heated iron.
But first, the iron is easier and better.
On cauterizing sores caused by an accident or a blow.
Chapter 48.
When there is pain in any limb caused by an accident or blow and the pain persists for a long time without healing with medicines, then it must be cauterized with a point cautery.
And let the iron be of a size proportionate to that of the limb and its thickness and weakness and strength and the place of the twisting and pain from it.
If therefore it heals with the first cauterization, it is well. If not, then repeat on it the cauterization.
For it is customary for these pains to shift from the limb to that which adjoins it. Why you must follow up on them with the iron until the patient is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in leprosy.
However, sometimes lepers benefit from the greatest aid of the iron. And especially the type of leprosy that occurs due to the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: when you wish to cauterize it, consider this.
If therefore the leprosy is in its beginning and you have treated it with that which we said in the division, and it has neither descended nor stopped, and you fear for the patient, lest corruption should spread over his entire complexion: then cauterize him on the head with five iron marks: one in the middle of the scalp; a second below it towards the front at the hairline; two above the two horns [temples], and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And with your hand holding the cautery for a short while, until it leaves on the bone a small impression and the chips are dislodged from it: so as to ease the exhalation of large vapors from this wound, cauterize also right above the spleen with the same cautery.
But if leprosy has already spread over the patient and appears manifestly, you should then cauterize with these same cauteries which we have mentioned in the head, one on the tip of the nose, two on both cheeks, two on the nape of the neck, six on the vertebrae of the back, and one large one above the coccyx and another over it itself at almeidati: and two on the hips - that is to say, a single one over each hip and two on the knees - one for every knee; and two on the shoulders, two on the elbows, two on the tenderness of his chest, and cauterize him also over all joint junctions, especially those of the fingers of both hands and feet: and cauterize too over both heel bones of their feet and palms of their hands.
Be careful to avoid the nerves which lie over the heel bone so as not to burn them.
Sometimes you must cauterize with one cautery over the breastbone, another over the stomach, and yet a third over the liver.
Know that the more you apply of the cautery, the greater is its benefit and efficacy.
And know that the patient will not experience pain from the cautery as healthy people do because their body is already numb.
And the cauteries ought to be of sizes and smallness suitable for limbs and joints as required by types of tools.
Then treat the cautery with herb flour and honey, and continue with the remaining treatment until it heals.
On how to cauterize for stupor.
When any member is stunned and treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but does not heal, then cauterize the stunned member with a cautery according to its size or smallness.
And let your cautery be as thick as the skin. Then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
Sometimes it is also cauterized for a kind of stupor that happens to the hand and foot, at the vertebrae of the back near where nerves emerge which move that member, and the stupor goes away.
But do not venture this unless you are knowledgeable about the anatomy of members and where the nerves emerge which move the body.
Chapter 51.
When albaras lasts long and you apply nothing from your medical skills to it: then cauterize right on it with a deep cautery according to the thickness of the skin until its whiteness is removed and its colour changes.
Then treat it with herb flour and lentils with rose oil and arnoglossae leaves and pigeon blood and swallow blood; let there be equal parts of each one: mix all these things together and apply them on a cloth and let it stick in place until it heals.
On the method of cauterization for cancer.
When cancer is beginning, and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around its circumference, as if it were turning.
The wise have said that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
That does not seem right to me, because I fear that it may be ulcerated; and indeed I have seen this happen several times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around its circumference with a circle, as we have said; or with multiple cauteries.
On the method of cauterization for abscesses.
When someone has an abscess that is delayed in maturing, due to excessiveness causing it, or because of the age and little blood of the patient, or because of time constraints when you wish to hasten its maturation, then cauterize around its circumference with multiple small cauteries by puncturing. Then leave it be. For itself will hasten with its own maturation.
If you wish to make an opening in it with the cautery, then heat the cautery which is of this form.
And place it on the abscess until it penetrates the skin; and let the patient be from one who follows, so that his path may be alleviated.
Treat it until it is healed.
On the way of cauterizing a corrosive sore.
Chapter 54.
A corrosive sore is nothing but an ongoing corruption of the limb, and it corrodes itself; like a fire consumes dry wood.
If you see a corrosive sore in a place that can tolerate fire-based cautery, then use many hot cauterizing irons of different sizes and lengths, depending on what is suitable for the location of the sore.
Then cauterize it from all sides until you eradicate the entire corruption, leaving nothing of it remaining whatsoever.
After that, leave it for three days, then apply powdered sulfur mixed with oil over the cauterized areas until all scabs and any remaining corruption is eradicated.
Then treat it with ointments that generate flesh.
If you see healthy new flesh generated after three days with no sign of corruption, it is good.
And if not, then repeat the cautery over what remains of the corrupted areas.
A corrosive sore is sometimes treated with an acute medicine. For that medicine arises in the place of the cautery.
However, fire-based cautery provides quicker relief; and I have indeed mentioned its use with acute medicine previously - take that where it is needed.
On the way of cauterizing warts and corns.
Chapter 50.
Many times this disease occurs in the lower parts of the feet: it is a thick, filtered substance that injures the foot.
And indeed the cautery on them is according to two methods: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
As for the amount when using fire, make a flat cautery like an eagle's feather: it should be made of iron and sized to hold a nail on all sides; and let its edges be thin.
Then place it, heated, on a nail. Then turn the hand with the cautery around the nail until it reaches the depth of the nail; and leave it there for three days until it begins to discharge pus. Then plaster it with crushed wild apples mixed with salt; and leave the plaster on overnight. For it will indeed eradicate itself from its roots.
Then treat the place with flesh-generating ointment until it is healed.
If they are not converted and often occur on the surface of the body, especially on hands and feet; then apply to them cautery with hot water: you should take a pipe made of brass or iron or an eagle's feather; and place it on a nail or althelul. Then pour a small amount of hot water into the pipe; hold your hand and turn it with your thumb pressure for a moment so that the edge of the pipe is pressed against the root of the nail, allowing the hot water to reach deep down, to the root of the nail: and let the patient wait a little while over this application of hot water for about an hour.
Then release it, for the nail is pulled out with its roots.
Do this to one after the other until you have come across all of them that are in the body.
Then treat them after they have been removed with what generates flesh from the ointments.
On the method of cauterization in tremor.
When someone experiences tremors due to cold affecting the nerves or from quartan fever or other causes, you should cauterize with four or five cauteries on the dorsal vertebrae and one between each vertebra, one on their chest, and another on their abdomen.
For the tremors indeed calm down with an oily cautery, and the cure of a cold disease becomes hastened.
On the method of performing cauterization according to Al-Bahir.
Chapter 57.
Sometimes Al-Bahir's foul ones, that is to say, pustules which are formed from coarse corrupted matter, appear on the body.
So when they appear, it is necessary that you first cauterize over the entire head of the pustule with a fine myrtle wood cautery whose end has been ignited by fire. Or with the root of long aristo-luchia. Or with a disk-shaped cautery.
And sometimes they are cauterized while still emerging following this method, and do not increase but the superfluity which produced them is broken down and they heal.
However, it is necessary that this should be done after evacuation with bloodletting.
On the method of cauterizing the flowing blood from an artery in a wound.
